Summary of Latest Trends in Manufacturing AI Transformation (AX)

This analysis comprehensively examines recent AI adoption trends in the manufacturing industry and derives key insights.

A key trend is that AI technology is expanding beyond individual processes to encompass the entire manufacturing value chain. In semiconductor processes, yield optimization based on digital twins (simulation through virtual models) is being applied, while adaptive robots and physical AI are being utilized in complex processes to maximize productivity. Furthermore, the combination of generative design and 3D printing presents the possibility of sustainable customized production.

AI's influence extends beyond factories, leading to the establishment of autonomous supply chains and the activation of digital manufacturing marketplaces, providing opportunities to enhance supply chain visibility and efficiency. However, for a successful transformation, the establishment of enterprise-wide AI governance is essential, and managing external risks such as export controls, arising from technological hegemony competition, is also emerging as an important challenge.

Therefore, for a successful AX, it is urgent to move beyond fragmented technology adoption and establish an integrated strategy and governance system that encompasses the entire value chain.

Guangdong Province has proposed implementation measures for AI-manufacturing integration over three years, including model/computing vouchers, interest subsidies for equipment upgrades, modernization of factory networks (private 5G, Wi-Fi 6, TSN), and ecosystem cooperation with companies like Huawei and Tencent. Manufacturers should map their DX roadmap to support menus, proactively prepare ROI/KPIs, and immediately utilize vouchers to pursue PoCs in vision-based quality inspection, predictive maintenance, production scheduling, and energy optimization. Furthermore, they should incorporate edge-cloud data pipelines, OT security and data governance, and open standards (ONNX/OPC UA/MQTT) into their RFPs to minimize vendor lock-in. In strategic sectors such as robotics, biomedicine, and low-altitude aviation, joint demonstrations and the establishment of reference lines are key to early market capture.

Guangdong Province has presented practical measures for the integration of AI in manufacturing over three years, including attracting large-scale investment (20 billion RMB AI investment by 2027), modernizing factory networks, providing model and computing vouchers, and offering interest subsidies for equipment investment. Manufacturers can highly leverage support if they prioritize high-ROI tasks such as vision inspection, predictive maintenance, and scheduling, and prepare 5G/TSN-based networks and an edge-cloud data structure. Through the establishment of joint PoC/reference lines with Huawei and Tencent ecosystems, costs and risks can be reduced, and financial support can shorten the payback period for introducing high-cost automation/robotics. Opportunities for component/system integration are also expanding, targeting demand linked to growth sectors such as robotics, biomedicine, and low-altitude aviation.

An AI-based digital manufacturing platform accelerates engineering, procurement, and production decision-making by shortening the RFQ-to-order cycle and increasing price and lead time transparency through design upload, instant quotation, automatic DFM, and supplier matching. It detects design defects such as thickness/material early before production to reduce rework and scrap and increase FTY. Furthermore, it stabilizes OTD/PPM by standardizing quality and process standards with AI across a 10,000+ global vendor network. Key success factors include PLM/ERP/MES API integration, data governance, vendor-agnostic data lake ingestion of price, lead time, and quality results, and KPI management (RFQ lead time, DFM rejection rate, FTY, OTD variance).

The article shows that AI-based digital manufacturing marketplaces, like Xometry, can accelerate the entire procurement and manufacturing process and lower quality, cost, and delivery risks through design uploads, instant quotes, automated manufacturability reviews, and large-scale supplier matching. Its practical value lies in early detection of defects at the design stage to reduce defects and rework, and in mitigating the variability of multi-regional sourcing by standardizing quality criteria among suppliers using AI. A platform strategy that connects procurement silos, integration with PLM/ERP/MES, and data governance are key to success, and an approach to managing performance with KPIs such as RFQ lead time, FTY, OTD, and lead time variance is recommended.

ë””ì§€í„¸ íŠ¸ìœˆÂ·ì§€ëŠ¥í˜• ì—ì´ì „íŠ¸ì˜ ì„±ìˆ™ìœ¼ë¡œ ììœ¨ ê³µê¸‰ë§ì´ í˜„ì‹¤í™”ë˜ì—ˆìœ¼ë©°, ë©€í‹°í‹°ì–´ ê³µê¸‰ì—…ì²´ ë§¤í•‘ê³¼ BOM-ê´€ì„¸ ì—°ê³„ë¥¼ í†µí•´ ê´€ì„¸ ë³€í™”Â·ê³µê¸‰ì—…ì²´ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ë¥¼ ì‹¤ì‹œê°„ ê°ì§€í•˜ê³  í†µê´€Â·ì»´í”Œë¼ì´ì–¸ìŠ¤ë¥¼ ìë™í™”í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. ì œì¡° í˜„ì¥ì€ â€˜ê´€ì„¸ X%â†‘/í•­ë§Œ íì‡„â€™ ë“± í‘œì¤€ ì‹œë‚˜ë¦¬ì˜¤ì™€ KPI(OTD, COGS, Scope 3)ë¥¼ ì‚¬ì „ ì •ì˜í•˜ê³ , ìµœì‹  ë¹„ìš©Â·ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ í”„ë¡œí•„ ê¸°ë°˜ì˜ ë™ì  ì†Œì‹±Â·ë¼ìš°íŒ… ìë™ ì „í™˜ì„ guardrailÂ·ì˜ˆì™¸ ìŠ¹ì¸ ì²´ê³„ë¡œ ìš´ì˜í•˜ì„¸ìš”. ê¸°ëŒ€ íš¨ê³¼ëŠ” ë¦¬ë“œíƒ€ì„ 27% ë‹¨ì¶•, ìƒì‚°ì„± 25% í–¥ìƒ, ë³µêµ¬ì‹œê°„ 60% ë‹¨ì¶•, íƒ„ì†Œ 16% ê°ì¶•ìœ¼ë¡œ ë¹„ì¦ˆë‹ˆìŠ¤ ì¼€ì´ìŠ¤ê°€ ëª…í™•í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. With the maturity of digital twins and intelligent agents, autonomous supply chains have become a reality, and through multi-tier supplier mapping and BOM-tariff linkage, tariff changes and supplier risks can be detected in real-time, and customs clearance and compliance can be automated. Manufacturing sites should pre-define standard scenarios such as 'tariff X% increase/port closure' and KPIs (OTD, COGS, Scope 3), and operate the automatic switching of dynamic sourcing and routing based on the latest cost and risk profiles with a guardrail and exception approval system. The expected benefits are a 27% reduction in lead time, a 25% improvement in productivity, a 60% reduction in recovery time, and a 16% reduction in carbon emissions, making the business case clear.

This article presents a blueprint for autonomous supply chain operation to respond to external shocks such as tariff fluctuations and port disruptions. The UK's export controls and NSIA take the 'capability' and 'end-use' of manufacturing AI as core judgment criteria, and intangible transfers (including email, API, and cloud) of model weights, datasets, source code, etc., as well as IP license transactions, become subject to control and review. Global manufacturers must implement dual-use function mapping and comparison against strategic goods lists from the project's early stages, documentation (data origin, purpose, risk assessment), contractual end-use/re-export restrictions, geofencing, and minimization of access rights, and reflect license and NSIA review lead times in their product/investment roadmaps.
ìš”ì•½:Summary:
ì´ ê¸€ì€ ì˜êµ­ ìˆ˜ì¶œí†µì œ(ECO 2008), íŠ¹í—ˆ ë¹„ë°€ìœ ì§€(Section 22), NSIAê°€ AI ëª¨ë¸Â·ë°ì´í„°ì…‹Â·ì½”ë“œ ê°™ì€ ë¬´í˜• ìì‚°ì— ì–´ë–»ê²Œ ì ìš©ë˜ëŠ”ì§€ ì„¤ëª…í•œë‹¤. ì œì¡° í˜„ì¥ì—ì„œ ì¬ë£Œì„¤ê³„Â·ê³µì • ì‹œë®¬ë ˆì´ì…˜Â·ë””ì§€í„¸ íŠ¸ìœˆ ë“± AIê°€ êµ°ë¯¼ê²¸ìš© ì„±ëŠ¥ì„ ê°–ê±°ë‚˜ WMD ê´€ë ¨ ìš©ë„ë¡œ ì“°ì¼ ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ì„ ì¸ì§€í•˜ë©´, ëª¨ë¸ ê°€ì¤‘ì¹˜/ë°ì´í„°ì…‹ì˜ í•´ì™¸ ì´ì „ì€ ë¼ì´ì„ ìŠ¤ê°€ í•„ìš”í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆê³ , IP ë¼ì´ì„ ìŠ¤ ìì²´ë„ NSIA ì‹¬ì‚¬ ëŒ€ìƒì´ ë  ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤. ê³µê°œ ë°ì´í„° ê¸°ë°˜ ëª¨ë¸ë„ ê²°ê³¼ì˜ ê¸°ëŠ¥ì´ êµ°ë¯¼ê²¸ìš©ì´ë©´ í†µì œë  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŒì„ ê°•ì¡°í•œë‹¤. ì‹¤ë¬´ì ìœ¼ë¡œëŠ” ì´ˆê¸° ê¸°ìˆ  ìŠ¤í¬ë¦¬ë‹, í†µì œëª©ë¡ ëŒ€ì¡°, ê³„ì•½ìƒ ì—”ë“œìœ ìŠ¤Â·ì§€ì—­ ì œí•œ, ì ‘ê·¼ê¶Œí•œ/ì§€ì˜¤íœì‹±, ê·œì œê¸°ê´€ê³¼ì˜ ì„ ì œ ì†Œí†µ, ì¼ì •Â·ë¹„ìš© ë°˜ì˜ì´ í•µì‹¬ì´ë‹¤. ë¶ì•„ì¼ëœë“œëŠ” EU ê·œì • ì ìš©ìœ¼ë¡œ í†µì œê°€ ë” ë„“ì„ ìˆ˜ ìˆì–´ ì§€ì—­ë³„ ê·œì œ ì°¨ì´ì—ë„ ìœ ì˜í•´ì•¼ í•œë‹¤. This article explains how UK export controls (ECO 2008), patent secrecy (Section 22), and NSIA apply to intangible assets such as AI models, datasets, and code. In manufacturing settings, if the potential for AI in material design, process simulation, digital twins, etc., to have dual-use capabilities or be used for WMD-related purposes is recognized, the overseas transfer of model weights/datasets may require a license, and the IP license itself could also be subject to NSIA review. It is emphasized that even models based on public data can be controlled if the functionality of their output is dual-use. Practically speaking, initial technology screening, comparison with control lists, contractual end-use and regional restrictions, access control/geofencing, proactive communication with regulatory authorities, and incorporating timelines and costs are key. Northern Ireland, due to the application of EU regulations, may have broader controls, so attention must also be paid to regional regulatory differences.

As the vulnerability of domestic advanced manufacturing, such as electric vehicles, semiconductor equipment, and wind power, has been exposed due to China's rare earth export controls, immediately implement BOM-level rare earth (Dy/Tb/Nd) content mapping, automatic assessment of regulatory and export license impacts, and an essential mineral risk dashboard + AI early warning system (covering license delays, port congestion, price/exchange rate, and shipping capacity). Verify 30/60/90-day delay and 20-50% price surge scenarios with a digital twin, and combine long-term off-take agreements, multi-sourcing, public-private joint purchasing funds, urban mining/recycling (with Dy/Tb recovery KPIs for motors and batteries), and Dy-reduced magnet design to simultaneously mitigate cost, OTD, and ESG risks.

China's rare earth export controls directly pose a risk to key processes in Korean manufacturing, including electric vehicles, smartphones, wind power, and semiconductor equipment. Expanding the directions suggested in the article from an AX perspective, key execution points include: 1) BOM-level rare earth content mapping and automated compliance, 2) AI-based early warning and risk dashboards, 3) digital twin for price and lead time impact simulation, 4) long-term offtake/joint purchase and multi-sourcing strategies, 5) urban mining and used battery/motor recovery-refinement systems and traceability, and 6) material substitution and Dy reduction design optimization. Viewing rare earths as 'strategic assets,' establishing a self-healing supply chain through digitalization, circularization, and standardization is key to competitiveness.

Building constraint-based Smart Configuration (CPQ) even before AI, which integrates configuration logic, pricing, installed assets, and customer/contract data into a single knowledge base, enables error-free quotes and orders, rapid Quote-to-Order connection, upselling/cross-selling, and pricing consistency in an ETO/MTO environment. Compared to rule-based systems, constraint-based systems reduce rule explosion and maintenance costs, are flexible to product changes, and become the foundation for raising the upper limit of future price optimization, demand-supply synchronization, order-specific BOMs, and generative AI sales copilot performance. In terms of implementation, identifying duplicate/exception rules, constraint modeling for options and compatibility, integration with CRM/ERP/PLM, and establishing data governance are key.
ìš”ì•½:Summary:
ì´ ê¸€ì€ ì œì¡°ì‚¬ê°€ AIë¥¼ ì„±ê³µì ìœ¼ë¡œ ë„ì…í•˜ê¸° ìœ„í•´ ë¨¼ì € â€˜ìŠ¤ë§ˆíŠ¸ êµ¬ì„±(ì œì•½ ê¸°ë°˜ CPQ)â€™ì„ êµ¬ì¶•í•´ì•¼ í•œë‹¤ëŠ” ì ì„ ê°•ì¡°í•œë‹¤. ê·œì¹™ ê¸°ë°˜ êµ¬ì„±ì˜ í•œê³„(ê·œì¹™ í­ë°œ, ìœ ì§€ë³´ìˆ˜ ë¹„ìš©, ì •í™•ë„ ë¬¸ì œ)ë¥¼ ì§šê³ , ì œì•½ ê¸°ë°˜ìœ¼ë¡œ ì „í™˜í•˜ì—¬ êµ¬ì„± ë¡œì§Â·ê°€ê²©Â·ìì‚°Â·ê³ ê° ë°ì´í„°ë¥¼ ì—°ê²°í•˜ë©´ ê²¬ì  ì†ë„ì™€ ì •í™•ë„ë¥¼ ê°œì„ í•˜ê³  ì˜¤ë¥˜ ì—†ëŠ” ì£¼ë¬¸Â·ì—…ì…€ ì¶”ì²œê¹Œì§€ ê°€ëŠ¥í•¨ì„ ì„¤ëª…í•œë‹¤. íŠ¸ëŸ­ êµ¬ì„± ì˜ˆì‹œë¥¼ í†µí•´ ë³µì¡ ì œí’ˆì˜ í˜„ì‹¤ ì ìš© ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ì„ ë³´ì—¬ì£¼ë©°, ë„ì… ë‹¨ê³„ë³„ ì‹¤í–‰ í¬ì¸íŠ¸(í˜„í–‰ ê·œì¹™ ì§„ë‹¨, ì œì•½ ëª¨ë¸ë§, MDM/ERP/PLM ì—°ê³„, ë³€ê²½ê´€ë¦¬/í…ŒìŠ¤íŠ¸ ìë™í™”)ë¥¼ ì œì‹œí•œë‹¤. í•µì‹¬ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ì´ëŠ” í–¥í›„ AI ê°€ê²© ìµœì í™”Â·ìƒì„±í˜• ì½”íŒŒì¼ëŸ¿Â·ì£¼ë¬¸ë³„ BOM ìë™í™”ì˜ ì„±ëŠ¥ì„ ì¢Œìš°í•˜ëŠ” ê¸°ë°˜ ì‘ì—…ì´ë¼ëŠ” ì „ëµì  ì‹œì‚¬ì ì„ ì œê³µí•œë‹¤. This article emphasizes that manufacturers must first build 'Smart Configuration (Constraint-based CPQ)' to successfully adopt AI. It addresses the limitations of rule-based configuration (rule explosion, maintenance costs, accuracy issues), and explains that by switching to constraint-based configuration and linking configuration logic, pricing, asset, and customer data, it is possible to improve quote speed and accuracy, and enable error-free orders and up-sell recommendations. Through a truck configuration example, it demonstrates the real-world applicability for complex products and presents execution points for each implementation stage (current rule diagnosis, constraint modeling, MDM/ERP/PLM integration, change management/test automation). Crucially, this provides the strategic implication that it is foundational work that will determine the performance of future AI price optimization, generative copilot, and order-specific BOM automation.

In the accelerating trend of AI adoption in 2025, it is effective for Manufacturing AI Transformation (AX) to prioritize high-ROI use cases such as predictive maintenance, vision inspection, yield optimization, and demand/inventory synchronization with a PoCâ†’expansion phase-based roadmap, and to pursue partial automation for autonomous monitoring, automatic tuning of process parameters, and automatic MRO ordering by leveraging lightweight/domain-specific models and agentic AI. We present the investment priorities and risk management points for Manufacturing AX through macro trends such as the AI adoption trend across all industries, the proliferation of customized models, energy and human resource issues, and the rise of Agentic AI. 14. When misunderstanding meets artificial intelligence: the critical role ...

ì†ŒìŠ¤:Source: https://www.frontiersin.org/journals/psychology/articles/10.3389/fpsyg.2025.1637...
í†µí•© ì¸ì‚¬ì´íŠ¸:Consolidated Insight:
ì—°êµ¬ëŠ” ì¸ê°„-AI í˜‘ì—…ì—ì„œ â€˜ì •ë³´ ëˆ„ë½â€™ë³´ë‹¤ â€˜ëª¨í˜¸í•œ í‘œí˜„â€™ì´ ì‹ ë¢°ë¥¼ ë” í¬ê²Œ í›¼ì†í•˜ë©°, ê·¸ ì—¬íŒŒë¡œ ì˜ì‚¬ì†Œí†µ íš¨ìœ¨ê³¼ íŒ€ ì„±ê³¼ê°€ íŠ¹íˆ ì¸ê°„-AI íŒ€ì—ì„œ ë” í¬ê²Œ ì•…í™”ë¨ì„ ì‹¤ì¦í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì œì¡° AX ê´€ì ì—ì„œ HMI/ì½”ë´‡/ì±—ë´‡Â·MESì— ëª¨í˜¸ì„± ê°ì§€ì™€ ìë™ ëª…í™•í™” ì§ˆì˜ ê¸°ëŠ¥ì„ ë‚´ì¥í•˜ê³ , ì•ŒëŒÂ·ì‘ì—…ì§€ì‹œ í‘œí˜„ í‘œì¤€í™”(ê¸ˆì§€ì–´Â·í•„ìˆ˜ì •ë³´ ì²´í¬)ì™€ ì˜¤í•´ ê´€ë ¨ KPI(time-to-clarify, ëŒ€í™” í„´, ì¬ì‘ì—…ë¥ ) ëª¨ë‹ˆí„°ë§, ì‹ ë¢° ë³µêµ¬ í”„ë¡œí† ì½œ ë° ì •ê¸° í˜‘ì—… êµìœ¡ì„ ìš´ì˜í•˜ëŠ” ê²ƒì´ ì‹¤ì§ˆì  ê°œì„ ì„ ì œê³µí•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. The research empirically demonstrates that 'ambiguous expressions' damage trust more significantly than 'missing information' in human-AI collaboration, and consequently, communication efficiency and team performance are worsened more significantly, particularly in human-AI teams. From a manufacturing AX perspective, embedding ambiguity detection and automatic clarification query functions into HMI/cobots/chatbots/MES, standardizing the expression of alarms and work instructions (checking for forbidden words and essential information), monitoring misunderstanding-related KPIs (time-to-clarify, conversation turns, rework rate), and implementing trust recovery protocols and regular collaboration training provide practical improvements.
ìš”ì•½:Summary:
ì´ ì—°êµ¬ëŠ” ì¸ê°„-ì¸ê³µì§€ëŠ¥ íŒ€ì—ì„œ â€˜ì •ë³´ ëˆ„ë½â€™ë³´ë‹¤ â€˜ëª¨í˜¸í•œ í‘œí˜„â€™ì´ ì‹ ë¢°ë¥¼ ë” í¬ê²Œ ë–¨ì–´ëœ¨ë¦¬ê³ , ê·¸ ê²°ê³¼ ì»¤ë®¤ë‹ˆì¼€ì´ì…˜ íš¨ìœ¨ê³¼ ì„±ê³¼ê°€ ì•…í™”ëœë‹¤ëŠ” ì ì„ ì‹¤í—˜ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ë³´ì—¬ì¤ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì œì¡° í˜„ì¥ì—ì„œëŠ” HMI/ì½”ë´‡/ì±—ë´‡ì— ëª¨í˜¸ì„± ê°ì§€ì™€ ëª…í™•í™” ì§ˆë¬¸ì„ ê¸°ë³¸ ì¥ì°©í•˜ê³ , ì‘ì—…ì§€ì‹œÂ·ì•ŒëŒ ë¬¸êµ¬ì˜ ëª¨í˜¸ì–´ ê¸ˆì§€ì™€ í•„ìˆ˜ì •ë³´ ì²´í¬ë¥¼ ê°•ì œí•˜ëŠ” ê²ƒì´ íš¨ê³¼ì ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë˜í•œ ì˜¤í•´ í•´ì†Œ ì‹œê°„Â·ëŒ€í™” í„´ ìˆ˜Â·ì‹ ë¢° ì§€í‘œë¥¼ KPIë¡œ ê³„ì¸¡í•˜ê³ , ì˜¤ë¥˜ ì‹œ ì„¤ëª…-êµì •-ì¬ë°œë°©ì§€-ì´ë ¥ ê°€ì‹œí™”ë¡œ ì‹ ë¢° ë³µêµ¬ í”„ë¡œí† ì½œì„ ìš´ì˜í•´ì•¼ í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì•ˆì „Â·í’ˆì§ˆ í•µì‹¬ ê³µì •ì—ì„œëŠ” ëª¨í˜¸ ì‘ë‹µì„ ì°¨ë‹¨í•˜ê³  ìë™ ì—ìŠ¤ì»¬ë ˆì´ì…˜ì„ ì ìš©í•˜ë©°, ì˜¤í¼ë ˆì´í„° AI ë¦¬í„°ëŸ¬ì‹œ êµìœ¡ê³¼ íŒŒì¼ëŸ¿ ë‹¨ê³„ì˜ ëª¨í˜¸ì„± ìŠ¤íŠ¸ë ˆìŠ¤ í…ŒìŠ¤íŠ¸ë¥¼ í†µí•´ í˜„ì¥ ë„ì… ìœ„í—˜ì„ ì¤„ì¼ ìˆ˜ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. This study experimentally demonstrates that 'ambiguous expressions' reduce trust more significantly than 'missing information' in human-AI teams, consequently deteriorating communication efficiency and performance. In manufacturing sites, it is effective to equip HMIs/cobots/chatbots with ambiguity detection and clarification questions by default, and to enforce the prohibition of ambiguous language and checks for essential information in work instructions and alarm messages. Additionally, time to resolve misunderstandings, number of conversation turns, and trust indicators should be measured as KPIs, and a trust recovery protocol should be implemented in case of errors, including explanation, correction, prevention of recurrence, and history visualization. In critical safety and quality processes, ambiguous responses should be blocked and automatic escalation applied, and the risk of field deployment can be reduced through operator AI literacy training and ambiguity stress testing at the pilot phase.

The India SME AI Playbook presents immediate, actionable priorities for manufacturing sites: bridging cost gaps through procurement, inventory, and logistics optimization; improving quality and operational rates through predictive maintenance and process parameter optimization; simultaneously reducing costs and carbon emissions with AI-powered energy and resource management; enhancing working capital with financial AI; and shortening development periods through virtual simulation. The speed of AGI transition depends on computing bottlenecks and economics, so manufacturers should establish a roadmap to gradually expand AX, starting with processes where the cost per task is lower than labor costs. Make algorithm efficiency â€“ including model lightweighting, domain-specific architectures, and data curriculum â€“ and compute TCO management, which encompasses power, cooling, and space (cloud-on-premise mix, capacity contracts), key levers for cost reduction. It is practical to prioritize visual inspection and predictive maintenance, which can deliver short-term results, and to gradually transition for tasks like inference and complex planning by combining human-in-the-loop approaches with retraining.

The transition to AGI will be dictated more by computing resources and cost than by technical feasibility, determining the speed of automation. Manufacturers should prioritize adoption in areas where the cost per task demonstrably falls below labor costs, and they must reduce TCO through algorithmic efficiency strategies such as model lightweighting. Considering the slowdown in semiconductor performance/price improvement and energy/material bottlenecks, endogenize compute, power, and space costs into CAPEX, and recalibrate investment priorities by distinguishing between capability bottlenecks and compute bottlenecks for each task. Human-in-the-loop and retraining strategies to mitigate workforce impact, along with compute procurement (hybrid cloud/on-premise, long-term capacity contracts, energy optimization), also dictate competitive advantage.

The core value of this article is that it presents practical options for converting industrial process heat to an electricity- and materials-based system. Labelers/scanners, operator tablets, on-site smartphones, and BYOD on the manufacturing floor are at the forefront of AI-based social engineering (smishing, deepfakes, voice fraud). With 93% using genAI on mobile, 77% concerned about the success potential of AI-assisted phishing, and 80% experiencing mobile phishing attempts, the adoption of AI response controls remains low despite these high threats, resulting in a significant defense gap. The priority is to convert critical lines to COBO/COSU to block BYOD, ensure 100% MDM/UEM enrollment with conditional access and rapid patching, implement phishing-resistant MFA and regular training, apply mobile EDR/MTD, DLP, and genAI guardrails, and protect OEE and line utilization through OT/IT microsegmentation and guest SSID isolation.

This report shows with figures that human-centric attacks, such as AI-powered smishing and deepfakes, are rapidly becoming more sophisticated through mobile devices and, combined with on-site worker errors, create significant risks (93% mobile genAI usage, 77% concern about successful AI phishing, 80% experience with mobile phishing attempts). Manufacturing site application points: Prohibition of BYOD on critical lines and transition to COBO/COSU; full implementation of MDM/UEM and conditional access / patch SLA; introduction of FIDO2/Passkeys instead of SMS; suppression of data leakage with mobile EDR/MTD and DLP; strengthening genAI usage guardrails and training; separation of OT/IT networks and establishment of offline operating procedures. By managing KPIs such as MDM registration rate, simulated smishing click-through rate, and genAI policy compliance rate, downtime, insurance penalties, and reputational risks can be proactively reduced.

Dow achieved a 50% reduction in crashes and a 16% improvement in productivity, while ELARABY achieved a 60% reduction in inter-site traffic (900GB/day) and improved perceived M365 performance. In manufacturing sites, a strategy of identifying bottlenecks with endpoint and application telemetry and reducing delays for ERP/MES/PLM, large files, and remote collaboration through WAN/cloud acceleration is effective. By operationalizing boot time, app response, data transfer volume, and downtime as SLOs and continuously improving them in conjunction with SLA and ROI, AX performance can be rapidly achieved.

ë³´ê³ ì„œëŠ” ë³µêµ¬ ìì‹ ê° ëŒ€ë¹„ ì‹¤ì œ ì™„ì „ ë³µêµ¬ìœ¨ì´ 15%ì— ê·¸ì¹œë‹¤ëŠ” ì ì„ ê²½ê³ í•˜ë©°, ì œì¡°ì—…ì€ í…Œì´ë¸”íƒ‘+ì‹¤ë³µêµ¬ ë“œë¦´ê³¼ ë¶ˆë³€/ì—ì–´ê°­ ë°±ì—…ì„ í¬í•¨í•´ PLCÂ·SCADA ì„¤ì •ê¹Œì§€ ì£¼ê¸° ë°±ì—…í•˜ê³ , ìƒì‚°ì¤‘ë‹¨ì„ ì¤„ì´ëŠ” ë‹¨ê³„ì  ë³µêµ¬ ì‹œë‚˜ë¦¬ì˜¤ë¥¼ ë§ˆë ¨í•´ì•¼ í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë˜í•œ 88%ê°€ ìƒì„±í˜• AIë¥¼ ì“°ì§€ë§Œ ì ˆë°˜ë§Œ ì •ì±…ì„ ë³´ìœ í•˜ë¯€ë¡œ, ë¯¼ê°ì •ë³´ ê¸ˆì§€Â·ìŠ¹ì¸íˆ´ ëª©ë¡Â·ë¡œê¹…Â·ëª¨ë‹ˆí„°ë§ ë“± ì‹¤íš¨ì  AI ì‚¬ìš© ì •ì±…ì„ ì‹ ì†íˆ ë„ì…í•˜ê³ , ë”¥í˜ì´í¬Â·í”¼ì‹±ì— ëŒ€ë¹„í•œ ì½œë°± ê²€ì¦ê³¼ ë‹¤ì ê²°ì¬ë¥¼ í‘œì¤€í™”í•´ì•¼ í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ê³µê¸‰ë§ ê²½ë¡œ(25%ê°€ ì†Œí”„íŠ¸ì›¨ì–´ ë²¤ë” ê¸°ì›)ì— ëŒ€ë¹„í•´ SBOM ìš”êµ¬, ê³µê¸‰ì—…ì²´ ë³´ì•ˆí‰ê°€ì™€ íŒ¨ì¹˜/ì·¨ì•½ì  í†µì§€ SLA ê³„ì•½í™”, ìµœì†Œê¶Œí•œÂ·ë„¤íŠ¸ì›Œí¬ ì„¸ê·¸ë©˜í…Œì´ì…˜ì„ ê°•í™”í•˜ëŠ” ê²ƒì´ í•µì‹¬ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. The report warns that the actual full recovery rate is only 15% compared to recovery confidence, and manufacturing must implement periodic backups, extending to PLC and SCADA configurations, incorporating tabletop and live recovery drills and immutable/air-gapped backups, and prepare phased recovery scenarios to reduce production downtime. Additionally, while 88% use generative AI, only half have policies in place; therefore, effective AI usage policies, such as prohibiting sensitive information, approved tool lists, logging, and monitoring, must be promptly introduced, and callback verification and multi-party approval must be standardized to counter deepfakes and phishing. To address supply chain risks (25% originating from software vendors), demanding SBOMs, formalizing supplier security assessments and patch/vulnerability notification SLAs, and strengthening least privilege and network segmentation are key.
ìš”ì•½:Summary:
ê¸€ë¡œë²Œ ì„¤ë¬¸ì€ â€˜ë³µêµ¬ ìì‹ ê° ëŒ€ë¹„ ì‹¤ì œ ë³µêµ¬ ì—­ëŸ‰ì˜ ê²©ì°¨â€™ì™€ â€˜AIê°€ ì¦í­í•˜ëŠ” ê³µê²©Â·ë°ì´í„° ìœ ì¶œ ìœ„í—˜â€™ì„ ìˆ˜ì¹˜ë¡œ í™•ì¸ì‹œí‚µë‹ˆë‹¤. ì œì¡°ì‚¬ëŠ” 1) ë¶ˆë³€/ì—ì–´ê°­ ë°±ì—…ê³¼ ì‹¤ì „í˜• ë³µêµ¬ ë“œë¦´ë¡œ RTO/RPOë¥¼ ê²€ì¦, 2) GenAI ì‚¬ìš© ì •ì±…ê³¼ ë°ì´í„° ë¶„ë¥˜Â·ë§ˆìŠ¤í‚¹ìœ¼ë¡œ ìœ ì¶œ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ë¥¼ í†µì œ, 3) SBOMÂ·íŒ¨ì¹˜ SLAÂ·ì‚¬ê³  í†µì§€ ì˜ë¬´ ë“± ê³µê¸‰ë§ ë³´ì•ˆ ìš”ê±´ì„ ê³„ì•½í™”, 4) ë”¥í˜ì´í¬Â·ì§€ë¶ˆ ì‚¬ê¸° ë°©ì§€ë¥¼ ìœ„í•œ ì½œë°± ê²€ì¦Â·ë‹¤ì ê²°ì¬ë¥¼ í‘œì¤€í™”, 5) OT/IT ì„¸ê·¸ë¨¼íŠ¸Â·MFAÂ·OT ì„¤ì • ë°±ì—… ë“± ì œì¡° íŠ¹í™” í†µì œë¥¼ ê°•í™”í•´ì•¼ í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. 2026ë…„ íˆ¬ì ìš°ì„ ìˆœìœ„(í´ë¼ìš°ë“œ ë³´ì•ˆ, ë°±ì—…, ì‚¬ìš©ì êµìœ¡)ë¥¼ ë³´ë“œ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ KPIì™€ ì—°ë™í•´ ê°­ì„ ë©”ìš°ëŠ” ì ‘ê·¼ì´ ì‹¤íš¨ì ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. A global survey quantifies 'the gap between recovery confidence and actual recovery capability' and 'the risks of attacks and data breaches amplified by AI'. Manufacturers must 1) verify RTO/RPO with immutable/air-gapped backups and practical recovery drills, 2) control data exfiltration risks with GenAI usage policies and data classification and masking, 3) contractualize supply chain security requirements such as SBOMs, patch SLAs, and incident notification obligations, 4) standardize callback verification and multi-party approval to prevent deepfake and payment fraud, and 5) strengthen manufacturing-specific controls such as OT/IT segmentation, MFA, and OT configuration backups. An effective approach is to bridge the gap by linking 2026 investment priorities (cloud security, backup, user training) with Board Risk KPIs.

This report suggests that, triggered by CSRD, manufacturing AI transformation (AX) must establish joint governance of CSR, IT, and Finance, a standardized ESG data model (linked with ERP/PLM/IoT), and internalize Scope 3 through supply chain traceability and vendor data collection. In practice, while expanding the use of AI for report automation, data integrity/anomaly detection, Scope 3 estimation, and labeling/traceability, etc., it is necessary to simultaneously pursue ethical AI governance involving the CSR department and the alignment of security and personal information policies. Implementation Points: Supply chain data programs and vendor onboarding, incorporation of double materiality-based KPIs and internal carbon pricing into performance management, establishment of LLM-based reporting assistants and validation rule sets, and change management operations.

With the implementation of Europe's CSRD, ESG data is being elevated to a strategic asset, and for manufacturing, joint governance of CSR-IT-Finance and an integrated data architecture are key. Focusing on purchasing, supply chain, and IT functions, they should promote the strengthening of Scope 3 and traceability, and by leveraging AI, they can enhance reporting automation, data anomaly detection, and Scope 3 estimation efficiency. Since the biggest obstacles are lack of personnel/time and conflicting priorities, implementation capabilities must be secured by introducing financially linked mechanisms such as distributed governance, function-specific capability building, and internal carbon pricing. An AI ethics, environmental, and psychosocial risk management framework is also essential to implement in parallel.

Amid geopolitical and macroeconomic changes, a shift from JIT to JIC is required, and operational design reflecting safety stock, dual/multi-sourcing, and lead time fluctuations, along with decision-making that includes a risk premium in TCO, is necessary. To operate regionally fragmented value chains with AI and automation, leverage demand forecasting, production scheduling, risk sensing, and digital twins to enhance visibility and decision-making speed, and defend unit costs through automation during reshoring. In preparation for tariffs, export controls, exchange rates, and the possibility of a weaker dollar, strengthen compliance governance, implement multi-currency settlement and hedging, diversify markets and supply chains to regions like ASEAN/India through a 'China+1' strategy, and execute continuous scenario planning.

This article emphasizes that global supply chains are being structurally reorganized by geopolitics, tariffs, and export controls, and that AI promotes region-centric, fragmented value chains. The manufacturing industry should transition from JIT to JIC, strengthening safety stock, alternative sourcing, and regional dualization, and operate complex networks with AI-based demand forecasting, scheduling, and risk sensing. In preparation for the potential weakening of dollar dominance, it is necessary to prepare for multi-currency settlement, foreign exchange risk management, and digital currency pilots, and in an Asia strategy, combining 'China+1' with domestic market-focused diversification is effective. During reshoring, shifting the cost structure through automation and making scenario planning, including sanctions, tariffs, and logistics disruptions, and compliance governance a continuous practice are presented as practical tasks.

Geelong is an example where, through a triple-helix collaboration among local government, industry, and Deakin University, a commercialization pipeline from R&D â†’ pilot â†’ spin-off â†’ mass production and a university testbed were established, lowering the risk of introducing AI/digital transformation in manufacturing and accelerating its adoption. As AI transformation accelerates and the complexity of real-time pipelines and unstructured data processing increases, manufacturing AX must elevate data engineering to a partner in business decision-making and expand investment in capabilities. To scale AI on the manufacturing floor, a high-quality, real-time, and consistent single data foundation is key, and this forms the foundational infrastructure for smart factories. Practically, reliability and low-latency decision-making can be ensured through OT protocol standardization (OPC UA/MQTT), semantic models for process, equipment, and quality data (ISA-95/88), event-driven streaming and data governance, and edge-cloud architecture integrated with MLOps. Through this, one can expect predictive maintenance, process optimization, improved throughput, reduced quality variability, and enhanced energy efficiency.

The launch of CSCMS provides a platform that accelerates the verification and commercialization of Industry 4.0/AI technologies through collaboration between industry, academia, research institutions, and government, supporting widespread adoption by linking industrial partnerships and the startup ecosystem. The CSCMS launch event is a networking and demo-centric event that provides a point of contact for industry-academia-government collaboration for smart manufacturing and AI transformation. Although specific technical and case study information is limited, it provides an opportunity to understand technology maturity, integration difficulty, and industry priority challenges, and to design low-cost pilots through lab tours and partner panels. The flow of capital into AI supplier convertible bonds suggests it's time to assess the status of key vendors, such as semiconductor and HPC infrastructure providers, and explore strategic sourcing and partnership (selective investment) opportunities. In preparation for circumvention exports of Chinese products due to the maintenance/strengthening of Trump-style tariffs and deflationary pressure in Asia, proactively implement CoO (Country of Origin) tracking and enhanced compliance, diversified routing, contract redesign including price linkage and renegotiation triggers, and production and inventory optimization based on demand elasticity. Furthermore, similar to the JPMorgan case, it is effective to introduce an AI copilot for purchasing, demand forecasting, and risk monitoring to advance procurement and CAPEX decision-making based on exchange rate, interest rate, and tariff scenarios.

JPMorgan suggested paying attention to related convertible bonds, stating that the benefits of the AI boom are concentrated in the supply chain (semiconductors, components, infrastructure). Simultaneously, due to US-China tariff risks, an increase in transshipments from China and rising deflationary pressures in Asia, strengthening of certificates of origin and compliance, price-linked contracts, and adjustments to CAPEX and FX hedging timing are necessary. A slowdown in Asian inflation could increase the possibility of easing borrowing costs, presenting an opportunity for financial strategy, while an asset management case (Spectrum GPT) can be utilized as a benchmark for the adoption of decision-making AI copilots in manufacturing.

Trends in technology licensing fees from government-funded research institutes are market signals that gauge industrial demand and commercialization maturity. Manufacturers should prioritize engaging with fast-growing institutions like ETRI to pursue IP licensing/joint development focused on Smart Factory, 5G/Edge, and Industrial AI. After screening based on TRL and ROI criteria, they must ensure effective execution through line PoC, scale-up, and KPI monitoring of yield, OEE, and defect rates. Collaboration portfolios with institutions showing decreasing royalty income need to be re-evaluated and redesigned based on demand-driven projects and on-site pilots.

ETRI has proven its commercialization capabilities by significantly increasing its technology royalty income over the past three years, while some government-funded research institutes showed a decrease. Manufacturers can utilize this as a signal of changing technology demand to realign their scouting priorities and strengthen licensing and joint development in smart factory, telecommunications/AI fields with growing organizations like ETRI. Incentive-friendly contracts that consider the royalty distribution structure (60% to researchers, 10% to contributors), along with evaluations based on TRL, ROI, and integration difficulty, a PoC-Scale-up roadmap, and a KPI tracking system, can increase the success rate of adoption.
